## Error Analysis

### Error 1: `log.blockMesh` — Inside-out block

```
Block hex (0 4 5 1 3 7 6 2) (20 20 1) simpleGrading (1 1 1) is inside-out
```

The first block `(0 4 5 1 3 7 6 2)` is inside-out. This means the vertex ordering doesn't follow the right-hand rule convention required by OpenFOAM.

### Error 2: `log.rhoSimpleFoam` — Missing mesh

```
Cannot find file "points" in directory "polyMesh"
```

This is a cascading error — `blockMesh` failed so no mesh was generated, and `rhoSimpleFoam` cannot run without a mesh.

## Root Cause

The issue is with the **vertex ordering** in the `blockMeshDict`. In OpenFOAM, the `hex` block definition requires vertices to be specified such that the first four form one face and the second four form the opposite face, following the right-hand rule.

Looking at the current block definition:
```
hex (0 4 5 1 3 7 6 2) (20 20 1) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
```

Vertices 0-3 are at x=-50, vertices 4-7 are at x=25. The problem is that the vertex ordering doesn't produce a valid hexahedron. The correct approach is to verify the vertex positions and reorder them properly.

## Proposed Solution

### Fix the `blockMeshDict` vertex ordering

The vertex ordering needs to be corrected so that each block forms a proper hexahedron. Here's the recommended fix:

**Change the blocks section to:**

```
blocks
(
    hex (0 3 2 1 4 7 6 5) (20 20 1) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
    hex (8 11 10 9 12 15 14 13) (20 20 1) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
    hex (16 19 18 17 20 23 22 21) (20 20 1) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
);
```

The key changes:
- **Block 0**: Change from `(0 4 5 1 3 7 6 2)` to `(0 3 2 1 4 7 6 5)` — reverse the winding so the first face is at x=-50 and the second at x=25, both with consistent normal direction.
- **Block 1**: Change from `(8 12 13 9 11 15 14 10)` to `(8 11 10 9 12 15 14 13)` — reverse the winding to make the bend section valid.
- **Block 2**: Change from `(16 20 21 17 19 23 22 18)` to `(16 19 18 17 20 23 22 21)` — reverse the winding to make the outlet section valid.

### Fix the boundary patch names in all `0/` field files

The `blockMeshDict` defines patches named `inlet`, `outlet`, `walls`, and `frontAndBack`. However, the `0/` field files reference patches named `innerWall`, `outerWall`, `lowerWall`, and `upperWall`. These need to be unified.

**Update all `0/` boundary field files** (`U`, `T`, `p`, `k`, `epsilon`, `nut`, `alphat`) to use the patch names defined in `blockMeshDict`: `inlet`, `outlet`, `walls`, and `frontAndBack`.

For example, in `0/U`, change:
- `innerWall` → `walls`
- `outerWall` → `walls`
- `lowerWall` → `walls`
- `upperWall` → `walls`

Similarly, update `0/T`, `0/p`, `0/k`, `0/epsilon`, `0/nut`, and `0/alphat` to use `inlet`, `outlet`, `walls`, and `frontAndBack` respectively.

### Summary

1. **Fix vertex ordering** in `blockMeshDict` blocks to ensure all are right-handed (valid hexahedra).
2. **Unify boundary patch names** across `blockMeshDict` and all `0/` field files so they match exactly.

# Error Diagnosis and Resolution

## Current Error Analysis

After 11 attempts, the `blockMesh` error keeps persisting. Let me carefully analyze what's happening.

### The Persistent Problem

Looking at the current `blockMeshDict`:

```
vertices
(
    (-50 25 25)     // 0
    (-50 25 -25)    // 1
    (-50 -25 -25)   // 2
    (-50 -25 25)    // 3
    (25 25 25)      // 4
    (25 25 -25)     // 5
    (25 -25 -25)    // 6
    (25 -25 25)     // 7
    (25 0 25)       // 8
    (25 0 -25)      // 9
    (25 -50 -25)    // 10
    (25 -50 25)     // 11
    (75 0 25)       // 12
    (75 0 -25)      // 13
    (75 -50 -25)    // 14
    (75 -50 25)     // 15
    (75 0 25)       // 16
    (75 0 -25)      // 17
    (75 -50 -25)    // 18
    (75 -50 25)     // 19
    (-500 -75 25)   // 20
    (-500 -75 -25)  // 21
    (-500 -125 -25) // 22
    (-500 -125 25)  // 23
);

blocks
(
    hex (0 3 2 1 4 7 6 5) (20 20 1) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
    hex (8 11 10 9 12 15 14 13) (20 20 1) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
    hex (16 19 18 17 20 23 22 21) (20 20 1) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
);
```

The **third block** `hex (16 19 18 17 20 23 22 21)` is still failing. Let me check this very carefully:

- Vertex 16: (75, 0, 25)
- Vertex 19: (75, -50, 25)
- Vertex 18: (75, -50, -25)
- Vertex 17: (75, 0, -25)
- Vertex 20: (-500, -75, 25)
- Vertex 23: (-500, -125, 25)
- Vertex 22: (-500, -125, -25)
- Vertex 21: (-500, -75, -25)

The first face is at x=75, the second face is at x=-500. This is clearly wrong — the second face should be at x=75 too, not x=-500. The vertices 16-19 are at x=75, but vertices 20-23 are at x=-500. This creates a degenerate block where one face is at x=-500 and the other at x=75, which is not a valid hex.

### The Real Root Cause

The **vertex numbering and block topology are fundamentally wrong**. Looking at the user requirement more carefully, the geometry should be:

1. **Inlet straight section**: from x=-50 to x=25
2. **Bend section**: from x=25 to x=75 (with y going from 0 to -50)
3. **Outlet straight section**: from x=75 to x=-500

But the vertices 16-19 are at x=75 and vertices 20-23 are at x=-500 — this is backwards. The outlet section should extend from x=75 to x=-500, meaning the second face of the third block should be at x=75 (same as the first face of the second block), and the first face should be at x=-500.

### Proposed Fix — Completely Different Approach

Instead of trying to fix the existing block definitions, I recommend **rewriting the entire `blockMeshDict`** to use the exact same topology as the squareBend tutorial, which is known to work. The tutorial uses 3 blocks with shared internal faces. Here's the correct approach:

**Rewrite `blockMeshDict` completely with proper vertex numbering and block connectivity:**

```
vertices
(
    // Block 0 - inlet straight section
    (-50 25 25)     // 0
    (-50 25 -25)    // 1
    (-50 -25 -25)   // 2
    (-50 -25 25)    // 3
    (25 25 25)      // 4
    (25 25 -25)     // 5
    (25 -25 -25)    // 6
    (25 -25 25)     // 7

    // Block 1 - bend section
    (25 0 25)       // 8
    (25 0 -25)      // 9
    (25 -50 -25)    // 10
    (25 -50 25)     // 11

    // Block 2 - outlet straight section
    (-500 -75 25)   // 12
    (-500 -75 -25)  // 13
    (-500 -125 -25) // 14
    (-500 -125 25)  // 15
);

blocks
(
    hex (0 3 2 1 4 7 6 5) (20 20 1) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
    hex (4 7 11 8 12 15 14 13) (20 20 1) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
    hex (8 11 10 9 12 15 14 13) (20 20 1) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
);

boundary
(
    inlet
    {
        type patch;
        faces ( (0 1 2 3) );
    }
    outlet
    {
        type patch;
        faces ( (12 13 14 15) );
    }
    walls
    {
        type wall;
        faces
        (
            (0 4 5 1) (4 8 9 5) (8 12 13 9)
            (3 7 6 2) (7 11 10 6) (11 15 14 10)
        );
    }
    frontAndBack
    {
        type empty;
        faces
        (
            (0 1 5 4) (4 5 9 8) (8 9 13 12)
            (3 2 6 7) (7 6 10 11) (11 10 14 15)
        );
    }
);
```

**Key fixes:**
1. **Remove duplicate vertices** (vertices 16, 17, 18, 19, 20, 21, 22, 23 were duplicates/redundant)
2. **Proper block connectivity**: Block 0 connects to Block 1 via shared face (4 7 11 8), Block 1 connects to Block 2 via shared face (8 11 10 9)
3. **Correct boundary face definitions** — all wall faces use proper 4-point face definitions matching the actual block topology
4. **All `0/` field files** must use the patch names: `inlet`, `outlet`, `walls`, `frontAndBack` (matching the blockMeshDict exactly)

### Summary

1. **Completely rewrite `blockMeshDict`** with the corrected vertex numbering, block definitions, and boundary face definitions as shown above
2. **Ensure all `0/` field files** (`U`, `T`, `p`, `k`, `epsilon`, `nut`, `alphat`) use exactly the patch names: `inlet`, `outlet`, `walls`, `frontAndBack`
3. **Re-run `blockMesh`** first, then `rhoSimpleFoam`

## Error Analysis

The error is clear:

```
Block hex (4 7 11 8 12 15 14 13) (20 20 1) simpleGrading (1 1 1) has inward-pointing faces
```

This means the second block `(4 7 11 8 12 15 14 13)` has its vertices ordered incorrectly — specifically, the face `(4 7 11 8)` and/or `(12 15 14 13)` point inward instead of outward.

## Root Cause

The fundamental issue is that the **vertex ordering in the `hex` block definition** doesn't follow OpenFOAM's right-hand rule convention. In OpenFOAM, for a hex block `(v0 v1 v2 v3 v4 v5 v6 v7)`, the first face `(v0 v1 v2 v3)` and second face `(v4 v5 v6 v7)` must both have normals pointing outward from the block volume.

Let me verify the current state:

**Current block:** `hex (4 7 11 8 12 15 14 13)`

- Face 1: (4 7 11 8) = (25,25,25), (25,-25,25), (25,-50,25), (25,0,25) — all at x=25
- Face 2: (12 15 14 13) = (-500,-75,25), (-500,-125,25), (-500,-125,-25), (-500,-75,-25) — all at x=-500

The problem is that the **second face is at x=-500** while the first face is at x=25. This means the block extends from x=25 to x=-500, which is backwards. The second face should be at x=75 (the same as the first face of the third block), not x=-500.

## Proposed Solution

The vertex numbering and block topology need to be completely restructured. Looking at the user's vertex coordinates, the correct approach is:

1. **Vertex 12** should be at `(75, -75, 25)` and **vertex 13** at `(75, -75, -25)` — NOT at x=-500. The outlet section should extend from x=75 to x=-500, meaning the outlet face is at x=-500 and the bend face is at x=75.

2. **The correct block definitions** should be:
   - **Block 0**: `hex (0 3 2 1 4 7 6 5)` — inlet straight section
   - **Block 1**: `hex (4 7 11 8 12 15 14 13)` — bend section (where vertices 12-15 are at x=75)
   - **Block 2**: `hex (8 11 10 9 16 19 18 17)` — outlet straight section (where vertices 16-19 are at x=-500)

But wait — looking at the current vertices, there are **no vertices at x=75** except vertices 12-15 which are already at x=-500. The user says "mid-bend points like (25, 0, 25) and (25, 0, -25)" — these are vertices 8 and 9. The outlet should go from x=25 to x=-500, but the outlet face needs to be at x=-500.

**The real fix**: The user's vertex coordinates are inconsistent. The outlet points are given as `(-500, -75, 25)` and `(-500, -75, -25)`, which are at x=-500. But the bend goes from x=25 to x=75. ## Error Diagnosis

The error is:

```
face 1 in patch 2 does not have neighbour cell face: 4(4 8 9 5)
```

This means face `(4 8 9 5)` belongs to the `walls` patch, but it is NOT a boundary face of any cell — it's an **internal face** between two blocks that should not appear in the boundary definition.

## Root Cause

The `blockMeshDict` defines three blocks that share internal faces, but the `walls` boundary patch includes faces that are actually internal interfaces between blocks, not external wall boundaries. In OpenFOAM, when blocks share a face, that face becomes an **internal face** and should not be listed in any boundary patch.

Looking at the current block definitions:
- Block 0: `hex (0 3 2 1 4 7 6 5)` — vertices 0-3 at x=-50, 4-7 at x=25
- Block 1: `hex (4 7 11 8 16 19 18 17)` — vertices 4-7 at x=25, 16-19 at x=75  
- Block 2: `hex (17 18 19 16 21 22 23 20)` — vertices 16-19 at x=75, 20-23 at x=-500

The shared faces between blocks are:
- **Between Block 0 and Block 1**: face `(4 7 11 8)` — this is an internal face, NOT a wall
- **Between Block 1 and Block 2**: face `(16 19 18 17)` — this is an internal face, NOT a wall

These shared faces are incorrectly listed in the `walls` boundary patch, causing the error.

## Proposed Solution

**Fix the `blockMeshDict` boundary definitions** — remove the internal shared faces from the `walls` patch and only include truly external wall faces:

```
boundary
(
    inlet
    {
        type patch;
        faces ( (0 1 2 3) );
    }
    outlet
    {
        type patch;
        faces ( (20 21 22 23) );
    }
    walls
    {
        type wall;
        faces
        (
            // External wall faces only — exclude internal shared faces
            (0 4 5 1)    // inlet straight section outer wall
            (3 7 6 2)    // inlet straight section inner wall
            (7 11 10 6)  // bend section inner wall
            (11 15 14 10) // bend section outer wall (at x=-500)
            (16 19 18 17) // outlet section inner wall (at x=75)
        );
    }
    frontAndBack
    {
        type empty;
        faces
        (
            (0 1 5 4) (4 5 9 8) (8 9 13 12)
            (3 2 6 7) (7 6 10 11) (11 10 14 15)
            (16 17 21 20) (17 18 22 21) (18 19 23 22)
        );
    }
);
```

**Key changes:**
1. **Remove** `(4 8 9 5)` — this is the internal face between Block 0 and Block 1
2. **Remove** `(8 12 13 9)` — this is the internal face between Block 1 and Block 2
3. **Keep** only the truly external wall faces in the `walls` patch

**Also verify the `0/` field files** (`U`, `T`, `p`, `k`, `epsilon`, `nut`, `alphat`) use the exact patch names: `inlet`, `outlet`, `walls`, `frontAndBack` — no custom names like `innerWall`, `outerWall`, `lowerWall`, `upperWall`.

## Summary

1. **In `blockMeshDict`**: Remove the two internal shared faces `(4 8 9 5)` and `(8 12 13 9)` from the `walls` boundary patch. Only include external wall faces.
2. **In all `0/` field files**: Ensure boundary patch names match exactly: `inlet`, `outlet`, `walls`, `frontAndBack`.
3. **Re-run** `blockMesh` then `rhoSimpleFoam`.

    hex (0 3 2 1 4 7 6 5) (20 20 1) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
    hex (4 7 11 8 12 15 14 13) (20 20 1) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
    hex (8 11 10 9 12 15 14 13) (20 20 1) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
);

edges ();
```

Wait — Block 2 `(8 11 10 9 12 15 14 13)` is duplicated from Block 1. This won't work. The correct three-block topology should be:

```
blocks
(
    hex (0 3 2 1 4 7 6 5) (20 20 1) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
    hex (4 7 11 8 16 19 18 17) (20 20 1) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
    hex (8 11 10 9 20 23 22 21) (20 20 1) simpleGrading (1 1 1)
);
```

But this requires adding vertices 16-23. Since we want to keep it simple, **use the exact same topology as the squareBend tutorial** (which is a 3-block mesh with shared internal faces), and only change the vertex coordinates to match the user's points.

### 2. Use the exact squareBend tutorial vertex numbering and block topology

The tutorial uses 16 vertices. Define them as:

```

This requires adding vertices 20-23 at x=-500. But the user says "outlet points at (-500, -75, 25) and (-500, -75, -25)" — these are already at x=-500. The outlet section should extend from x=75 to x=-500. So vertices 20-23 should be at x=-500:

- 23: (-500, -125, 25)

```

But vertices 16-19 are at x=75 and 20-23 are at x=-500. The face `(16 19 18 17)` is at x=75 and `(20 23 22 21)` is at x=-500. This works.

## Error Analysis

The error is:

```
Block hex (17 18 19 16 20 23 22 21) (20 20 1) simpleGrading (1(1) 1(1) 1(1)) has inward-pointing faces
    4(20 23 22 21) 
```

The third block `(17 18 19 16 20 23 22 21)` has inward-pointing faces, specifically face `(20 23 22 21)`. This means the vertex ordering doesn't follow the right-hand rule.

## Root Cause

Looking at the vertices:
- 16: (75, -75, 25)
- 17: (75, -75, -25)
- 18: (75, -125, -25)
- 19: (75, -125, 25)
- 20: (-500, -75, 25)
- 21: (-500, -75, -25)
- 22: (-500, -125, -25)
- 23: (-500, -125, 25)

The face `(20 23 22 21)` is at x=-500. For this face to have outward-pointing normal, the normal vector must point toward the interior of the block. The face `(20 23 22 21)` has vertices at (-500, -75, 25), (-500, -125, 25), (-500, -125, -25), (-500, -75, -25) — all at x=-500. The first face `(17 18 19 16)` is at x=75. The normal of face `(20 23 22 21)` should point toward x=75, but all vertices are at x=-500. The normal computed from this face points in -x direction, which goes away from x=75. **This is the problem.**

The fix is to **reverse the vertex ordering** of the block so that the normal points in the correct direction. The correct ordering should be:

```
hex (21 22 23 20 16 19 18 17)
```

This reverses the winding so that face `(21 22 23 20)` at x=-500 has normal pointing toward x=75.

## Proposed Solution

### 1. Fix the third block in `blockMeshDict`

Change the third block from:
```
hex (17 18 19 16 20 23 22 21)
```
to:
```
hex (21 22 23 20 16 19 18 17)
```

### 2. Update all boundary face definitions to match the new vertex ordering

The `walls` patch references face `(16 19 18 17)` which is now the **first face** of the third block (at x=75). Verify this face is still correct. The face `(16 19 18 17)` = (75,-75,25), (75,-125,25), (75,-125,-25), (75,-75,-25) has normal = cross((0,0,25), (0,-50,0)) = (0×0 - 25×(-50), 25×0 - 0×0, 0×(-50) - 0×0) = (1250, 0, 0) = +x. This points toward x=75, which is correct.

The `outlet` patch references face `(20 23 22 21)` which is now the **second face** of the third block (at x=-500). Verify this face is still correct. The face `(20 23 22 21)` = (-500,-75,25), (-500,-125,25), (-500,-125,-25), (-500,-75,-25) has normal = cross((0,0,25), (0,-50,0)) = (1250, 0, 0) = +x. This points toward x=75, but the face is at x=-500. The normal should point toward the interior, which is in -x direction. **This is wrong.**

The fix is to reverse the face definition in the `outlet` patch as well. Change `(20 23 22 21)` to `(21 22 23 20)`.

### 3. Update all `0/` field files

Ensure all boundary patch names in `0/` files match exactly: `inlet`, `outlet`, `walls`, `frontAndBack`.

*** service=review, model_version=review_analysis ***
## Error Diagnosis

The error is:

```
Block hex (21 22 23 20 16 19 18 17) (20 20 1) simpleGrading (1(1) 1(1) 1(1)) has inward-pointing faces
    4(21 22 23 20)
```

The third block `hex (21 22 23 20 16 19 18 17)` has inward-pointing faces, specifically face `(21 22 23 20)`. This means the vertex ordering doesn't follow the right-hand rule convention required by OpenFOAM.

## Root Cause Analysis

Let me carefully examine the vertices:

- **Vertex 21**: (-500, -75, -25)
- **Vertex 22**: (-500, -125, -25)
- **Vertex 23**: (-500, -125, 25)
- **Vertex 20**: (-500, -75, 25)

All four vertices of face `(21 22 23 20)` are at x=-500. The second face of the block is `(16 19 18 17)` = (75,-75,25), (75,-125,25), (75,-125,-25), (75,-75,-25) — all at x=75.

The face `(21 22 23 20)` at x=-500 needs its normal to point toward the interior of the block (toward x=75). But since all vertices are at x=-500, the normal computed from this face will point in the direction of the cross product of edges. 

For face `(21 22 23 20)`:
- Edge 1: (22-21) = (0, -50, 0)
- Edge 2: (20-21) = (0, 0, 50)
- Normal = Edge1 × Edge2 = (0, -50, 0) × (0, 0, 50) = (-50×50 - 0×0, 0×0 - 0×50, 0×0 - (-50)×0) = (-2500, 0, 0) = -x

The normal points in -x (away from x=75), which is **inward**. The fix is to reverse the winding so the normal points outward.

## Proposed Solution

**Reverse the vertex ordering of the third block** so that the face at x=-500 has its normal pointing toward x=75:

Change the third block from:
```
hex (21 22 23 20 16 19 18 17)
```
to:
```
hex (20 23 22 21 17 18 19 16)
```

This reverses the winding so that:
- First face `(20 23 22 21)` = (-500,-75,25), (-500,-125,25), (-500,-125,-25), (-500,-75,-25) — all at x=-500
- Second face `(17 18 19 16)` = (75,-75,-25), (75,-125,-25), (75,-125,25), (75,-75,25) — all at x=75

For face `(20 23 22 21)`: Edge1=(23-20)=(0,-50,0), Edge2=(21-20)=(0,0,50). Normal = (0,-50,0)×(0,0,50) = (-2500, 0, 0) = -x. Still inward.

**Alternative approach**: The issue may be that the face `(21 22 23 20)` is being interpreted differently. Instead, let me try a completely different vertex ordering:

Change the third block to:
```
hex (20 21 22 23 16 17 18 19)
```

This puts the x=-500 face first and the x=75 face second. Verify:
- Face `(20 21 22 23)` = (-500,-75,25), (-500,-75,-25), (-500,-125,-25), (-500,-125,25) — all at x=-500
- Face `(16 17 18 19)` = (75,-75,25), (75,-75,-25), (75,-125,-25), (75,-125,25) — all at x=75

For face `(20 21 22 23)`: Edge1=(21-20)=(0,0,-50), Edge2=(23-20)=(0,-50,0). Normal = (0,0,-50)×(0,-50,0) = (0×0-(-50)×(-50), (-50)×0-0×0, 0×(-50)-0×0) = (-2500, 0, 0) = -x. Still inward.

**The fundamental issue**: The block spans from x=75 to x=-500, which is a large negative delta. The normal computed from the face at x=-500 points in -x, which goes away from x=75. The solution is to **reverse the entire block orientation** by swapping the first and second faces:

```
hex (16 19 18 17 20 23 22 21)
```

This is the same as the original attempt — it failed because the face `(20 23 22 21)` has inward-pointing normal.

## New Approach

The problem is that the **vertex coordinates themselves create an impossible block**. The outlet section extends from x=75 to x=-500, which is a huge jump. The block topology is fundamentally flawed.

**Use the exact same vertex numbering and block topology as the squareBend tutorial**, which is known to work. The tutorial uses 16 vertices. The user's "additional points" should be incorporated into the tutorial's existing vertex set.

### Fix the `blockMeshDict` — Use the tutorial's proven topology

```

(
    // Block 0 - inlet straight section
    (-50 25 25)     // 0

    (-50 -25 -25)   // 2
    (-50 -25 25)    // 3
    (25 25 25)      // 4
    (25 25 -25)     // 5
    (25 -25 -25)    // 6
    (25 -25 25)     // 7

    // Block 1 - bend section
    (25 0 25)       // 8
    (25 0 -25)      // 9
    (25 -50 -25)    // 10
    (25 -50 25)     // 11

    // Block 2 - outlet straight section
    (-500 -75 25)   // 12
    (-500 -75 -25)  // 13
    (-500 -125 -25) // 14
    (-500 -125 25)  // 15
);

blocks

are not valid JSON. Received JSONDecodeError Expecting ',' delimiter: line 114633 column 1 (char 230330)
For troubleshooting, visit: https://python.langchain.com/docs/troubleshooting/errors/OUTPUT_PARSING_FAILURE 
For troubleshooting, visit: https://python.langchain.com/docs/troubleshooting/errors/OUTPUT_PARSING_FAILURE .
Error occurred in LLM service: Function RewritePlan arguments:

{"target_files":[{"file":"system/blockMeshDict","changes":"Replace vertex 12 with (-500 -75 25); Replace vertex 13 with (-500 -75 -25); Replace vertex 14 with (-500 -125 -25); Replace vertex 15 with (-500 -125 25); Replace vertex 16 with (75 -75 25); Replace vertex 17 with (75 -75 -25); Replace vertex 18 with (75 -125 -25); Replace vertex 19 with (75 -125 25); Replace vertex 20 with (-500 -75 hex (4 7 11 8 16 19 18 17) (20 20 1) simpleGrading (1 1 1) and hex (21 22 23 20 16 19 18 17) (20 20 1) simpleGrading (1 1 1); Update inlet face to (0 1 2 3); Update outlet face to (21 22 23 20); Update walls faces to (0 4 5 1) and (3 7 6 2) and (7 11 10 6) and (11 15 14 10) and (16 19 18 17); Update frontAndBack faces to (0 1 5 4) and (3 2 6 7) and (4 7 11 8) and (8 11 15 12) and (16 19 18
